Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH Well Evaluation
INTRODUCTION
The Liberty Resource Management, LLC. - Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH [SE SE Section 17,
T158N-R95W] well is located approximately 7.3 miles north of Tioga in Williams County,
North Dakota. It will expand the existing McGregor Field situated along the western flank of the
Nesson anticline (Figure 1). This well includes five wells to be batch drilled on the same pad,
and is the fifth vertical-curve section and first lateral section of the pad. The Gohrick 158-95-17-
8-6MBH is a double-section, horizontal Middle Bakken Member well within the Williston Basin,
consisting of one ~9,822' long lateral drilled to the north at a proposed azimuth of 2.28º. The
curve will be kicked off in the Lodgepole Formation and landed within the Middle Bakken
Member. Directional drilling and geo-steering techniques would then be used to maintain
maximum exposure to the target zone.
Figure 1. GIS map of well location, existing wells and fields. (NDIC, GIS map server, 2014)
GEOLOGY
Lithology
Lithology descriptions and sample analysis began at the base of the Otter Formation in order to
log the top of the Kibbey Formation. Formation tops and marker were used for curve landing
purposes, comparing these tops to select offset wells surrounding the surface location.
The Middle Bakken Member was logged at 9,575' TVD (-7,102' MSL). It consists primarily of
silty sandstone with a packstone layer of variable thickness, at the top of and including some of
the target zone. The target zone generally contained fine intergranular porosity and trace to rare
amounts of even brown oil staining (Figure 2).
Figure 2. Middle Bakken Member, silty sandstone (Steve Holzworth, Sunburst Well-site Geologist)
Curve Landing
Data including rate of penetration (ROP), torque, and lagged samples were used to determine
marker and formation tops during the vertical hole. Measurement-while-drilling (MWD) gamma
data was utilized in addition during the curve build. During both the vertical and curve, tops were
compared to our primary offset wells, in order to ensure a successful landing in the target zone.
The true vertical depth (TVD) of our initial landing target (9,609' TVD) was calculated by
assuming comparable formation thicknesses from the Base Last Salt marker bed to the landing
target. A decision was made to adjust the target to 9,605' TVD reaching the "Lodgepole X"
Marker. No further adjustments were made to the landing target and directional successfully
landed the curve at 9,607' TVD, at the base of the target interval.
Geosteering
The ideal target zone was defined as a 28' interval, the top of which was initially set at 9,582'
TVD, 7' below the base of the Upper Bakken Shale. The most useful signature for steering
purposes was a superimposed warm gamma marker, reading 85-110 (API) counts, below a cool
gamma marker, reading 40-65 (API) counts, positioned near the middle of the ideal target zone.
Offset wells indicated that structure would be up-dipping, at approximately +0.15° from entry of
the formation to total depth. The final gross overall rise in TVD from entry of the Middle Bakken
Member to the end of the lateral was estimated at 18' over 9,800', resulting in a gross apparent
dip of +0.10°. The bottom-hole location is estimated to be 10,067.98' north & 365.64' west of
surface location or approximately 241.44' FNL & 594.36' FEL, NE NE Section 8, T158N,
R95W. Geo-steering techniques exposed 80% of uncased borehole to the 28' middle Bakken
ideal target. The well reached a total depth of 19,682' on August 11, 2014 (Figure 3).
Figure 3. Cross-sectional interpretation of the Gohrick 6MBH well showing high gamma associated with the silty
sandstone intervals and low gamma within the packstone intervals. (Steve Holzworth, Sunburst well site geologist)
Hydrocarbons
Background gas fluctuated between 200 units and 1,500 units throughout the lateral. The highest
gas value recorded was a gas show at 18,126' MD, producing 2,532 units. The entire ideal target
zone was observed to contain relatively moderate gas concentrations and consistent oil staining.
The highest gas concentrations were seen between 16,000' MD to 19,000' MD correlating with
the middle of our ideal target zone (Figure 4).
Figure 4. Profile of the Gohrick 6MBH well with background gas in the range of 200-1,000 units. (S. Holzworth, Sunburst well site geologist)
SUMMARY
1)
The Liberty Management Resources, LLC. Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH was spud on
July 16, 2014, and reached total depth in 18 drilling days on August 11, 2014.
2)
Samples from the Middle Bakken target consisted of primarily of silty sandstone, a
packstone of varying thickness, and both with fair intergranular and intercrystalline
porosity. Oil shows in samples were visible as even trace to rare brown oil stain, which
yielded encouraging fluorescent cuts.
3)
Moderate gas shows were present throughout the lateral portion of the well, ranging
between 200 and 1,500 units, with the most significant gas show of 2,532 units occurring
at 18,126' MD.
4)
The Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH awaits completion operations to maximize its
production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Steve Holzworth
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
August 11, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught 30' sample intervals from 7,240' to 19,682' (TD). Formation tops and lithology markers have
been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference. Sample descriptions begin at the base of the
Mississippian, Otter Formation through the Bakken Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry under a
binocular microscope. Sample fluorescence cuts are masked by invert mud through intermediate casing. Quantifiers
in order of abundance are trace, rare, occasional, common and abundant.
Kibbey Formation [Mississippian; Big Snowy Group]
7,263' MD / 7,256' TVD (-4,783')
7240-7270 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray to gray-brown, friable, blocky, rare SANDSTONE: light pink,
orange-tan, very fine grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture
7270-7300 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray to gray-brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange-tan, very fine
grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture
7300-7330 SILTSTONE: light pink red, tan, light gray to gray-brown; SANDSTONE: cream to light pink, orange-
tan, very fine grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: red, common red to brown,
rare dark gray, soft to firm, blocky, earthy texture
7330-7360 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray to gray-brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange-tan, very fine
grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture, trace SHALE: orange, dark gray, blocky, friable, earthy
texture, slightly calcareous
7360-7390 SHALE: red orange, blocky, soft to firm, trace SILTSTONE: as above
Kibbey Lime [Mississippian Big Snowy Group]
7,399' MD / 7,392' TVD (-4,919')
7390-7420 LIMESTONE: cream to light gray, mudstone to wackestone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard,
crystalline
7420-7450 LIMESTONE: cream to light gray, mudstone to wackestone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm to hard,
crystalline
7450-7480 SILTSTONE: light orange, light to medium orange brown, blocky, mostly soft, occasionally friable,
rarely firm, slightly calcareous, anhydritic, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown to
cream, off white, soft, earthy, amorphous texture
7480-7510 SILTSTONE: light orange, light to medium orange brown, blocky, mostly soft, occasionally friable,
rarely firm, slightly calcareous, anhydritic, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown to
cream, off white, soft, earthy, amorphous texture
7510-7540 SILTSTONE: light orange, light to medium orange brown, blocky, mostly soft, occasionally friable,
rarely firm, slightly calcareous, anhydritic, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown to
cream, off white, soft, earthy, amorphous texture
Charles Formation: 1st Salt [Mississippian; Madison Gp.] 7,550' MD / 7,543' TVD (-5,070')
7540-7570 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral to subhedral, firm to hard, crystalline texture, no visible
porosity; ANHYDRITE: white, cream, amorphous, very soft, earthy texture, no visible porosity
7570-7600 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral to subhedral, firm to hard, crystalline texture, no visible
porosity; ANHYDRITE: white, cream, amorphous, very soft, earthy texture, no visible porosity
7600-7630 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral to subhedral, firm to hard, crystalline texture, no visible
porosity; ANHYDRITE: white, cream, amorphous, very soft, earthy texture, no visible porosity
7630-7660 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral to subhedral, firm to hard, crystalline texture, no visible
porosity; LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, trace brown, firm, crystalline, argillaceous in part,
dolomitic in part, trace dolomite, no visible porosity
7660-7690 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, trace brown, firm, crystalline, argillaceous in part,
dolomitic in part, trace dolomite, no visible porosity
7690-7720 ANHYDRITE: milky, soft, amorphous in part; ARGILLACEOUS LIMESTONE: medium to dark gray,
dense, crystalline, no visible porosity
7720-7750 SALT: clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral, crystalline; ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange,
tan, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: medium gray, light gray, occasional light brown, mudstone, microcrystalline,
soft, dense
7750-7780 SALT: clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral, crystalline; ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange,
tan, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray, light gray, occasional light brown, microcrystalline,
soft, dense
7780-7810 SALT: clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral, crystalline; ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange,
tan, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray, light gray, occasional light brown, microcrystalline,
soft, dense
7810-7840 SALT: clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral, crystalline
7840-7870 SALT: clear, rare milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral, crystalline; ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange,
tan, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray, light gray, occasional light brown, microcrystalline,
soft, dense
7870-7900 LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray, light gray, occasional light brown, microcrystalline, soft, dense;
occasional ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange, tan, soft, amorphous
7900-7930 ANHYDRITE: off white, light orange, tan, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray,

Dear Terry:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24759, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on the condition that all
portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east &
west boundaries within the 1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 8 & 17 T158N R95W. **The W/2 SW/4 of Section 8 is within both the
McGregor and Temple Fields. Tool error is not required pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on
the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration
operations are conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire location. Be advised the 20401 JV-
P Gohrick 43-17 well is within 8 feet of the proposed wellbore for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well. Precautions must be taken while
designing the frac job for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well as to not adversely affect the 20401 JV-P Gohrick 43-17 well. Be advised the M.C.
Gohrick 43-17 well is within 72 feet of the proposed wellbore for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well. Precautions must be taken while
designing the frac job for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well as to not adversely affect the M.C. Gohrick 43-17 well. LIBERTY RESOURCES
MANAGEMENT COMPANY, LLC must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous
operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator,
or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any producing well or oil tank." Be advised the 20401 JV-P Nelson 33-8 well is within 8 feet of
the proposed wellbore for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well. Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job for the Gohrick 158-95-
17-8-6MBH well as to not adversely affect the 20401 JV-P Nelson 33-8 well. Be advised the 20401 JV-P Hoseth 41-17 well is within 17 feet of the
proposed wellbore for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-6MBH well. Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job for the Gohrick 158-95-17-8-
6MBH well as to not adversely affect the 20401 JV-P Hoseth 41-17 well. LIBERTY RES MNGMT CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector
Tom Delling at 701-770-8660 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion operations, providing
the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud
system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings
and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional plan is at a legal
location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10109'N and 460'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit on the NDIC -
OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity
Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that would allow the Director to conclude
that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon
the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be
included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to
12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Terry L. Hoffman

Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys
with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director.
However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a certification cover page to
certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement utilized on
production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones can be determined,
(2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be
determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run
prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

Alice Webber

April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

STATEMENT
According to NDAC Section 43-02-03-19.2 and as outlined in the NDIC letter dated
4/9/14, Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC plans to abide with the filtration
container requirement for oil and gas operations on their Gohrick multi-well pad
location (SESE Section 17-T158N-R95W, Williams County, ND, which includes the
following wells:
Gohrick 158-95-17-8-4MBH
